FIFA World Cup Match Predictions Using Neural Networks¶

Baseline Models - Multiclass Logistic Regression and Simple Multilayer Perceptron on FIFA Rankings

CS109A¶

Nathan Goldberg, Erik Johnsson, James Weichert

July, 2018

In [5]:
#Separate into a predictor DataFrame and response variable column
y_train = fifa_df['Win']

#Drop the response variable from the predictor DataFrame. Also drop 'Type', as the baseline models will not take
#the type of game into account
X_train = fifa_df.drop(['Type', 'Win'], axis=1)
In [6]:
y_train = pd.DataFrame(y_train)

#Make a copy of the current state of y_train for use in Logistic Regression (which requires a different kind of 
#categorical encoding than the neural network)
y_train_cat = y_train.copy()

W = np.array(np.zeros(len(y_train)))
D = np.array(np.zeros(len(y_train)))
L = np.array(np.zeros(len(y_train)))

#Convert the {0, 0.5, 1} values in the response variable to one-hot encoded columns for win (home win), draw, and loss
#(away win)
for y in range(len(y_train)):
    if y_train.iloc[y].Win == 1:
        W[y] = 1
    elif y_train.iloc[y].Win == 0.5:
        D[y] = 1
    elif y_train.iloc[y].Win == 0:
        L[y] = 1

#Add the one-hot encoded columns to the response variable DataFrame and delete the original 'Win' column
y_train['W'] = W
y_train['D'] = D
y_train['L'] = L

y_train = y_train.drop(['Win'], axis=1)

Baseline Model #1: Multiple Logistic Regression¶

In [9]:
#Create the multinomial logistic regression model and fit it to the training data
logistic_model = LogisticRegression(solver='newton-cg', multi_class='multinomial')
logistic_model.fit(X_train, y_train_cat)

Baseline Model #2: Neural Network (Basic Multilayer Perceptron Using Keras)¶

In [11]:
#Create keras neural network model
model = Sequential()
In [12]:
#Add layers to the network
model.add(Dense(units=31, activation='relu', kernel_initializer='random_uniform', input_dim=31))
model.add(Dense(units=24, activation='relu', kernel_initializer='random_uniform'))
model.add(Dense(units=16, activation='relu', kernel_initializer='random_uniform'))
model.add(Dense(units=8, activation='relu', kernel_initializer='random_uniform'))
#Since this is a classification problem (win, draw, loss), a softmax will be used as the final activation
model.add(Dense(units=3, activation='softmax', kernel_initializer='random_uniform'))
In [20]:
cb = keras.callbacks.TensorBoard(log_dir='./logs', histogram_freq=0, batch_size=32, write_graph=True, write_grads=False, write_images=False, embeddings_freq=0, embeddings_layer_names=None, embeddings_metadata=None, embeddings_data=None)
In [21]:
#Compile the model using categorical cross-entropy as a loss function with a categorical_accuracy metric. Use the 
#'adam' optimizer for faster convergence on a minimum
model.compile(loss='categorical_crossentropy',
              optimizer='adam',
              metrics=['categorical_accuracy'])
In [22]:
#Train the model
model.fit(X_train, y_train, epochs=1000, batch_size=20,verbose=1, callbacks=[cb], validation_split = .2)
print("Done")

y_test = fixtures_fifa_df['Win']

Logistic Regression¶

In [17]:
#Predict the logistic regression model on the test set
reg_predictions = logistic_model.predict(X_test)
In [18]:
#Count how many times the prediction is correct and print the percentage of correct predictions
reg_correct_predictions = 0

for i in range(len(y_test)):
    if (y_test.iloc[i] == reg_predictions[i]/2):
        reg_correct_predictions += 1

print("Logistic Regression Prediction Accuracy: {0}%".format(100*reg_correct_predictions/len(y_test)))

Logistic Regression Prediction Accuracy: 0.5625%

In [21]:
#Convert the on-hot encoding back into a single column
results = [0]*len(predictions)

for i in range(len(predictions)):
    if(predictions.iloc[i].Win > predictions.iloc[i].Draw and predictions.iloc[i].Win > predictions.iloc[i].Loss):
        results[i] = 1
    elif(predictions.iloc[i].Draw >= predictions.iloc[i].Win and predictions.iloc[i].Draw >= predictions.iloc[i].Loss):
        results[i] = 0.5
    elif(predictions.iloc[i].Loss > predictions.iloc[i].Win and predictions.iloc[i].Loss > predictions.iloc[i].Draw):
        results[i] = 0
In [22]:
#Count how many times the prediction is correct and print the percentage of correct predictions
nn_correct_predictions = 0

for i in range(len(y_test)):
    if (y_test.iloc[i] == results[i]):
        nn_correct_predictions += 1

print("Neural Network Prediction Accuracy: {0}%".format(100*nn_correct_predictions/len(y_test)))

Neural Network Prediction Accuracy: 0.53125%

Trivial Model - Predict All Games as Home Wins¶

In [23]:
#Count how many times the prediction is correct and print the percentage of correct predictions
trivial_correct_predictions = 0

for i in range(len(y_test)):
    if (y_test.iloc[i] == 1):
        trivial_correct_predictions += 1

print("Trivial Model - Predict All Games as Home Wins. Prediction Accuracy: {0}%".format(100*trivial_correct_predictions/len(y_test)))

Trivial Model - Predict All Games as Home Wins. Prediction Accuracy: 0.40625%

#Separate into a predictor DataFrame and response variable column
y_train_wiggo = wiggo_df['Win']

In [6]:
X_train_wiggo.shape
Out[6]:
(6170, 31)
In [7]:
y_train_wiggo = pd.DataFrame(y_train_wiggo)

#Make a copy of the current state of y_train for use in Logistic Regression (which requires a different kind of 
#categorical encoding than the neural network)
y_train_cat_wiggo = y_train_wiggo.copy()

W = np.array(np.zeros(len(y_train_wiggo)))
D = np.array(np.zeros(len(y_train_wiggo)))
L = np.array(np.zeros(len(y_train_wiggo)))

#Convert the {0, 0.5, 1} values in the response variable to one-hot encoded columns for win (home win), draw, and loss
#(away win)
for y in range(len(y_train_wiggo)):
    if y_train_wiggo.iloc[y].Win == 1:
        W[y] = 1
    elif y_train_wiggo.iloc[y].Win == 0.5:
        D[y] = 1
    elif y_train_wiggo.iloc[y].Win == 0:
        L[y] = 1

#Add the one-hot encoded columns to the response variable DataFrame and delete the original 'Win' column
y_train_wiggo['W'] = W
y_train_wiggo['D'] = D
y_train_wiggo['L'] = L

y_train_wiggo = y_train_wiggo.drop(['Win'], axis=1)

In [10]:
#Create keras neural network model
wiggo_model = Sequential()
In [24]:
#Add layers to the network
wiggo_model.add(Dense(units=31, activation='relu', kernel_initializer='random_uniform', input_dim=31))
wiggo_model.add(Dense(units=24, activation='relu', kernel_initializer='random_uniform'))
wiggo_model.add(Dense(units=16, activation='relu', kernel_initializer='random_uniform'))
wiggo_model.add(Dense(units=8, activation='relu', kernel_initializer='random_uniform'))
#Since this is a classification problem (win, draw, loss), a softmax will be used as the final activation
wiggo_model.add(Dense(units=3, activation='softmax', kernel_initializer='random_uniform'))

keras.callbacks.TensorBoard(log_dir='./logs', histogram_freq=0, batch_size=32, write_graph=True, write_grads=False, write_images=False, embeddings_freq=0, embeddings_layer_names=None, embeddings_metadata=None, embeddings_data=None)
Out[24]:
<keras.callbacks.TensorBoard at 0x1232af128>
In [12]:
#Compile the model using categorical cross-entropy as a loss function with a categorical_accuracy metric. Use the 
#'adam' optimizer for faster convergence on a minimum
wiggo_model.compile(loss='categorical_crossentropy',
              optimizer='adam',
              metrics=['categorical_accuracy'])
In [13]:
#Train the model
wiggo_model.fit(X_train_wiggo, y_train_wiggo, epochs=1000, batch_size=20,verbose=1)
print("Done")

In [19]:
#Convert the on-hot encoding back into a single column
wiggo_results = [0]*len(wiggo_predictions)

for i in range(len(wiggo_predictions)):
    if(wiggo_predictions.iloc[i].Win > wiggo_predictions.iloc[i].Draw and wiggo_predictions.iloc[i].Win > wiggo_predictions.iloc[i].Loss):
        wiggo_results[i] = 1
    elif(wiggo_predictions.iloc[i].Draw >= wiggo_predictions.iloc[i].Win and wiggo_predictions.iloc[i].Draw >= wiggo_predictions.iloc[i].Loss):
        wiggo_results[i] = 0.5
    elif(wiggo_predictions.iloc[i].Loss > wiggo_predictions.iloc[i].Win and wiggo_predictions.iloc[i].Loss > wiggo_predictions.iloc[i].Draw):
        wiggo_results[i] = 0
In [20]:
#Count how many times the prediction is correct and print the percentage of correct predictions
nn_correct_predictions_wiggo = 0

for i in range(len(y_test_wiggo)):
    if (y_test_wiggo.iloc[i] == wiggo_results[i]):
        nn_correct_predictions_wiggo += 1

print("Neural Network Prediction Accuracy (WIGGO): {0}%".format(100*nn_correct_predictions_wiggo/len(y_test_wiggo)))

Neural Network Prediction Accuracy (WIGGO): 57.8125%
